class="mw-indicators mw-body-content">\n</div>\n<h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading" lang="en">Commonwealth realm</h1>\t\t\t<div id="bodyContent" class="mw-body-content">\n\t\t\t\t<div id="siteSub" class="noprint">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>\t\t\t\t<div id="contentSub"></div>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="jump-to-nav"></div>\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a>\n\t\t\t\t<a class="mw-jump-link" href="#p-search">Jump to search</a>\n\t\t\t\t<div id="mw-content-text" lang="en" dir="ltr" class="mw-content-ltr"><div class="mw-parser-output"><p class="mw-empty-elt">\n\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Commonwealth_realm_map.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Commonwealth_realm_map.svg/350px-Commonwealth_realm_map.svg.png" width="350" height="178" class="thumbimage" class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Commonwealth_realm_map.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #000080; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Commonwealth realms</div> <div class="legend" style="-webkit-column-break-inside: avoid;page-break-inside: avoid;break-inside: avoid-column"><span class="legend-color" style="display:inline-block; width:1.5em; height:1.5em; margin:1px 0; border:1px solid black; background-color: #0000FF; color:black; font-size:100%; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Overseas territories of Commonwealth realms</div></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_Hillsborough_Castle.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_Hillsborough_Castle.jpg/220px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_Hillsborough_Castle.jpg" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8c/Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_Hillsborough_Castle.jpg/330px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_Hillsborough_Castle.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/8/8c/Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_Hillsborough_Castle.jpg 2x" data-file-width="400" data-file-height="500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_at_Hillsborough_Castle.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> is the reigning sovereign of each of the 16 Commonwealth realms.</div></div></div>\n<p>A <b>Commonwealth realm</b> is a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a><sup id="cite_ref-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-1">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 1&#93;</a></sup> in which <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Queen Elizabeth II</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a> and reigning <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarch</a>. Each realm is independent from the other realms. As of 2018, there are 16 Commonwealth realms: <a href="/wiki/Antigua_and_Barbuda" title="Antigua and Barbuda">Antigua and Barbuda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Bahamas" title="The Bahamas">The Bahamas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Realm_of_New_Zealand" title="Realm of New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Kitts_and_Nevis" title="Saint Kitts and Nevis">Saint Kitts and Nevis</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lucia" title="Saint Lucia">Saint Lucia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. All 16 Commonwealth realms are members of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a>, an intergovernmental organisation of 53 <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Member states of the Commonwealth of Nations">member states</a>. Elizabeth II is <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">Head of the Commonwealth</a>.\n</p><p>In 1952, Britain\'s <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_accession_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Proclamation of accession of Elizabeth II">proclamation of Elizabeth II\'s accession</a> used the term <i>Realms</i> to describe the seven sovereign states of which she was queen\xe2\x80\x94the United Kingdom, Canada, Australia, New Zealand, <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">South Africa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan" title="Dominion of Pakistan">Pakistan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Ceylon</a>. Since then, new realms have been created through independence of former colonies and dependencies and some realms have become republics.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Current_Commonwealth_realms">Current Commonwealth realms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Current Commonwealth realms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>There are 16 Commonwealth realms currently with a combined area (excluding <a href="/wiki/Antarctic" title="Antarctic">Antarctic</a> claims) of 18.7&#160;million km<sup>2</sup> (7.2&#160;million mi<sup>2</sup>)<sup id="cite_ref-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup> and a population of 144&#160;million,<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> of which all but about two million live in the six most populous: the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">Jamaica</a>.\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable sortable">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Country<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;Note Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Niue" title="Niue">Niue</a> are under the sovereignty of the Queen of New Zealand as self-governing <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">states in free association</a> with New Zealand. New Zealand and its associated states, along with <a href="/wiki/Tokelau" title="Tokelau">Tokelau</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Ross_Dependency" title="Ross Dependency">Ross Dependency</a>, compose the <a href="/wiki/Realm_of_New_Zealand" title="Realm of New Zealand">Realm of New Zealand</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-12"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-12">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="Bailiwick of Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a>\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Crown_dependencies" title="Crown dependencies">Crown dependencies</a>\xe2\x80\x94are self-governing possessions of the British Crown, under the sovereignty of the Queen of the United Kingdom. Together with the UK, these comprise the <a href="/wiki/British_Islands" title="British Islands">British Islands</a>.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_of_the_realms">Relationship of the realms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Relationship of the realms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The Commonwealth realms are, for purposes of international relations, <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>. They are united only in their voluntary connection with the institution of the monarchy,<sup id="cite_ref-Trepanier28_14-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trepanier28-14">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> the succession, and the Queen herself; the person of the sovereign and the Crown were said in 1936 to be "the most important and vital link" between the realms.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> Political scientist Peter Boyce called this grouping of countries associated in this manner, "an achievement without parallel in the history of international relations or constitutional law."<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Terms such as <i><a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> a <i>form of personal union</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-Scott1_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Scott1-24">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 2&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-murdoch1_25-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murdoch1-25">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> and <i>shared monarchy</i>,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> among others,<sup id="cite_ref-Elliott1_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Elliott1-29">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 3&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-corbett1_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corbett1-30">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> have all been advanced as definitions since the beginning of the Commonwealth itself, though there has been no agreement on which term is most accurate,<sup id="cite_ref-sack1_28-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sack1-28">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-corbett1_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corbett1-30">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> or even whether <i>personal union</i> is applicable at all.<sup id="cite_ref-Miller1_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Miller1-32">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 4&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1926" title="Balfour Declaration of 1926">Balfour Declaration of 1926</a>, the realms have been considered "equal in status, in no way subordinate one to another in any aspect of their domestic or external affairs, though united by a common allegiance to the Crown."<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trepanier28_14-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trepanier28-14">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cox_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Mallory_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mallory-36">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trepanier144_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trepanier144-37">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> and the monarch is "equally, officially, and explicitly [monarch] of separate, autonomous realms."<sup id="cite_ref-Trepanier28_14-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trepanier28-14">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cox_35-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Trepanier144_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trepanier144-37">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> Andrew Michie wrote in 1952 "Elizabeth II embodies in her own person many monarchies: she is Queen of Great Britain, but she is equally Queen of Canada, Australia, New Zealand, Pakistan, South Africa, and Ceylon... it is now possible for Elizabeth II to be, in practice as well as theory, equally Queen in all her realms."<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Still, Boyce holds the counter-opinion the crowns of all the non-British realms are "derivative, if not subordinate" to the crown of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The United Kingdom no longer possesses any legislative power over any country besides itself, although some countries continue to use, by their own volition, the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> as part of their own judiciary; usually as the highest court of appeal.\n</p><p>Since each realm has the same person as its monarch, the diplomatic practice of exchanging <a href="/wiki/Ambassador" title="Ambassador">ambassadors</a> with <a href="/wiki/Letter_of_credence" title="Letter of credence">letters of credence and recall</a> from one head of state to another is redundant. Diplomatic relations between the Commonwealth realms are thus at a cabinet level only and <a href="/wiki/High_Commissioner_(Commonwealth)" class="mw-redirect" title="High Commissioner (Commonwealth)">high commissioners</a> are exchanged between realms (though all other countries in the Commonwealth of Nations also follow this same practice, but for traditional reasons). A high commissioner\'s full title will thus be <i>High Commissioner for Her Majesty\'s Government in [Country]</i>. For certain ceremonies, the order of precedence for the realms\' high commissioners or national flags is set according to the chronological order of, first, when the country became a Dominion and then the date on which the country gained independence.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Conflicts of interest have arisen from this relationship amongst independent states, ranging from minor diplomatic matters\xe2\x80\x94such as the monarch expressing on the advice of one of her <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinets</a> views that counter those of another of her cabinets<sup id="cite_ref-Conf_45-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Conf-45">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 5&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94to more serious conflicts regarding matters of armed conflict, wherein the monarch, as head of state of two different realms, may be simultaneously at war and at peace with a third country, or even at war with herself as head of two hostile nations.<sup id="cite_ref-War_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-War-46">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 6&#93;</a></sup> In such cases, viceroys have tended to avoid placing the sovereign directly in the centre of the conflict, meaning that a governor-general may have to take controversial actions entirely on his or her own initiative through the exercise of the <a href="/wiki/Reserve_powers" class="mw-redirect" title="Reserve powers">reserve powers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-GGs_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GGs-47">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 7&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In recent years, advocates have argued for free movement of citizens among a subset of the Commonwealth realms: the United Kingdom, Canada, Australia, and New Zealand, which they argue "share the same head of state, the same native language, [and] the same respect for the common law."<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> Opinion on the prospect of the plan coming to fruition is mixed.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> British <a href="/wiki/Euroscepticism" title="Euroscepticism">Eurosceptics</a> (those critical of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>) have expressed a preference for a relationship "similar in nature and goals to the EU" between the same four countries: the <a href="/wiki/CANZUK" title="CANZUK">CANZUK</a> Union without repeating the "mistakes of Europe"\xe2\x80\x94though this possibility has also been characterised as "difficult and in some ways far-fetched".<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Despite this, public opinion polling conducted by organisations such as <a href="/wiki/CANZUK_International" title="CANZUK International">CANZUK International</a> and <a href="/wiki/YouGov" title="YouGov">YouGov</a> have indicated widespread support for free movement of goods and people across Canada, Australia, New Zealand and the United Kingdom, with support for the proposals ranging from between 58\xe2\x80\x9364% in the United Kingdom, 70\xe2\x80\x9372% in Australia, 75\xe2\x80\x9377% in Canada and 81\xe2\x80\x9382% in New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Crown_in_the_Commonwealth_realms">The Crown in the Commonwealth realms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: The Crown in the Commonwealth realms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>The evolution of the Commonwealth realms has resulted in <a href="/wiki/The_Crown" title="The Crown">the Crown</a> having both a shared and a separate character, with the one individual being equally monarch of each state and acting as such in right of a particular realm as a distinct <a href="/wiki/Legal_person" title="Legal person">legal person</a> guided only by the advice of the <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_(government)" title="Cabinet (government)">cabinet</a> of that jurisdiction.<sup id="cite_ref-Trepanier28_14-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Trepanier28-14">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Cox_35-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-35">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Bogdanor_56-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bogdanor-56">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-HCUK_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCUK-57">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Toporoski_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toporoski-59">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> This means that in different contexts the term <i>Crown</i> may refer to the extra-national institution associating all 16 countries, or to the Crown in each realm considered separately.<sup id="cite_ref-Toporoski_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toporoski-60">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 8&#93;</a></sup> However, though the monarchy is therefore no longer an exclusively British institution,<sup id="cite_ref-Bogdanor_56-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bogdanor-56">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Toporoski_59-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toporoski-59">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> having become "domesticated" in each of the realms,<sup id="cite_ref-Mallory_36-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mallory-36">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> it may in the media and legal fields often still be elaborated as the <i>British Crown</i> for reasons historical, of convenience, or political, regardless of the different, specific, and official national <a href="/wiki/List_of_titles_and_honours_of_Queen_Elizabeth_II#Current" class="mw-redirect" title="List of titles and honours of Queen Elizabeth II">titles</a> and <a href="#Current_Commonwealth_realms">terms</a> used when addressing the Queen of the citizenry in each jurisdiction. For example, in <a href="/wiki/Barbados" title="Barbados">Barbados</a> the Queen is titled as <i>Elizabeth II, Queen of Barbados</i>, or simply the <i>Queen of Barbados</i>, with her full title making mention of her position as queen of the other Commonwealth realms.\n</p><p>From a cultural standpoint, the sovereign\'s name and image and other royal symbols unique to each nation are visible in the emblems and insignia of governmental institutions and militia. The Queen\'s effigy, for example, appears on coins and banknotes in some countries, and an oath of allegiance to the Queen is usually required from politicians, judges, military members and new citizens. By 1959, it was being asserted by Buckingham Palace officials that the Queen was "equally at home in all her realms."<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_succession_and_regency">Royal succession and regency</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Royal succession and regency">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>To guarantee the continuity of multiple states sharing the same person as monarch, the preamble of the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a> laid out a convention that any alteration to the <a href="/wiki/Succession_to_the_British_throne" title="Succession to the British throne">line of succession</a> in any one country must be voluntarily approved by the parliaments of all the realms.<sup id="cite_ref-SueHill_62-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SueHill-62">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 9&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-SOW_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SOW-63">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> This convention was first applied in 1936 when the British government conferred with the Dominion governments during the <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII_abdication_crisis" title="Edward VIII abdication crisis">Edward VIII abdication crisis</a>. Prime Minister of Canada <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a> pointed out that the Statute of Westminster required Canada\'s request and consent to any legislation passed by the British parliament before it could become part of Canada\'s laws and affect the line of succession in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-Twomey_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twomey-64">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Sir <a href="/wiki/Maurice_Gwyer" title="Maurice Gwyer">Maurice Gwyer</a>, <a href="/wiki/Office_of_the_Parliamentary_Counsel_(United_Kingdom)" title="Office of the Parliamentary Counsel (United Kingdom)">first parliamentary counsel</a> in the UK, reflected this position, stating that the Act of Settlement was a part of the law in each Dominion.<sup id="cite_ref-Twomey_64-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Twomey-64">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Though today the Statute of Westminster is law only in Canada, Australia, and the United Kingdom,<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> the convention of approval from the other realms was reasserted by the <a href="/wiki/Perth_Agreement" title="Perth Agreement">Perth Agreement</a> of 2011, in which all 16 countries agreed in principle to change the succession rule to <a href="/wiki/Absolute_primogeniture" class="mw-redirect" title="Absolute primogeniture">absolute primogeniture</a>, to remove the restriction on the monarch being married to a Catholic, and to reduce the number of members of the Royal Family who need the monarch\'s permission to marry. These changes came into effect on 26 March 2015. Alternatively, a Commonwealth realm may choose to cease being such by making its throne the inheritance of a different royal house or by becoming a republic, actions to which, though they alter the country\'s royal succession, the convention does not apply.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Agreement among the realms does not, however, mean the succession laws cannot diverge. During the abdication crisis in 1936, the United Kingdom passed <a href="/wiki/His_Majesty%27s_Declaration_of_Abdication_Act_1936" title="His Majesty&#39;s Declaration of Abdication Act 1936">His Majesty\'s Declaration of Abdication Act</a> with the approval of the parliament of Australia and the governments of the remaining Dominions. (Canada, New Zealand, and South Africa gave parliamentary assent later.<sup id="cite_ref-SydLaw_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydLaw-67">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup>) The Act effected Edward\'s abdication in the United Kingdom on 11 December; as the Canadian government had requested and consented to the Act becoming part of Canadian law, and Australia and New Zealand had then not yet adopted the Statute of Westminster, the abdication took place in those countries on the same day. The parliament of South Africa, however, passed its own legislation\xe2\x80\x94<a href="/wiki/His_Majesty_King_Edward_the_Eighth%27s_Abdication_Act,_1937" title="His Majesty King Edward the Eighth&#39;s Abdication Act, 1937">His Majesty King Edward the Eighth\'s Abdication Act, 1937</a>\xe2\x80\x94which backdated the abdication there to 10 December. The Irish Free State recognised the king\'s abdication with the <a href="/wiki/Executive_Authority_(External_Relations)_Act_1936" title="Executive Authority (External Relations) Act 1936">Executive Authority (External Relations) Act 1936</a> on 12 December.<sup id="cite_ref-SydLaw_67-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydLaw-67">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/Anne_Twomey" title="Anne Twomey">Anne Twomey</a>, this demonstrated "the divisibility of the Crown in the personal, as well as the political, sense."<sup id="cite_ref-SydLaw_67-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-SydLaw-67">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> For E H Coghill, writing as early as 1937, it proved that the convention of a common line of succession "is not of imperative force".<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup> and Kenneth John Scott asserted in 1962 that it ended the "convention that statutory uniformity on these subjects would be maintained in the parts of the Commonwealth that continued to owe allegiance to the Crown".<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Today, some realms govern succession by their own domestic laws, while others, either by written clauses in their constitution or by convention, stipulate that whoever is monarch of the United Kingdom is automatically also monarch of that realm. It is generally agreed that any unilateral alteration of succession by the UK would not have effect in all the realms.<sup id="cite_ref-Cox_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cox-74">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the accession of <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a> to the throne, the United Kingdom created <a href="/wiki/Regency_Acts#Regency_Act_1937" title="Regency Acts">legislation that provided for a regency</a> in the event that the monarch was not of age or incapacitated. Though input was sought from the Dominions on this matter, all declined to make themselves bound by the British legislation, feeling instead that the governors-general could carry out royal functions in place of a debilitated or underage sovereign.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a> later incorporated this principle into its constitution.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> New Zealand included in its <a href="/wiki/Constitution_Act_1986" title="Constitution Act 1986">Constitution Act 1986</a> a clause specifying that, should a regent be installed in the United Kingdom, that individual would carry out the functions of the monarch of New Zealand.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Monarch.27s_role_in_the_realms"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Monarch\'s_role_in_the_realms">Monarch\'s role in the realms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Monarch&#039;s role in the realms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The monarch holds the highest position in each Commonwealth realm and may perform such functions as issuing <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive orders</a>, commanding the military forces, and creating and administering laws.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> However, each country now operates under the <a href="/wiki/Westminster_system" title="Westminster system">Westminster system</a> of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_democracy" class="mw-redirect" title="Parliamentary democracy">parliamentary democracy</a> and the concept of <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a>, meaning that the monarch by convention exercises her powers on the <a href="/wiki/Advice_(constitutional)" title="Advice (constitutional)">advice</a> of her <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Crown" title="Minister of the Crown">Crown ministers</a>, who are usually drawn from, and thus responsible to, the <a href="/wiki/Election" title="Election">elected</a> chamber of the relevant <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>. In some realms, such as <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, these conventions are codified in constitutional law.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:RoyalVisitSenate.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/RoyalVisitSenate.jpg/220px-RoyalVisitSenate.jpg" width="220" height="275" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/RoyalVisitSenate.jpg/330px-RoyalVisitSenate.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bd/RoyalVisitSenate.jpg/440px-RoyalVisitSenate.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="751" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:RoyalVisitSenate.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Queen_Elizabeth_The_Queen_Mother" title="Queen Elizabeth The Queen Mother">Queen Elizabeth</a>, grants <a href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Assent">Royal Assent</a> to bills in the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Canada" title="Senate of Canada">Senate of Canada</a>, 1939</div></div></div>\n<p>The sovereign resides predominantly in her oldest realm, the United Kingdom, and thus carries out her duties there mostly in person. The Queen appoints <a href="/wiki/Viceroy" title="Viceroy">viceroys</a> to perform most of the royal constitutional and ceremonial duties on her behalf in the other realms: in each, a <a href="/wiki/Governor-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor-General">governor-general</a> as her personal national representative, as well as a <a href="/wiki/Governors_of_the_Australian_states" title="Governors of the Australian states">governor</a> as her representative in each of <a href="/wiki/States_and_territories_of_Australia" title="States and territories of Australia">the Australian states</a>. These appointments are all made on the advice of the prime minister of the country or the premier of the state concerned, though this process may have additional requirements.<sup id="cite_ref-Viceroy_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Viceroy-79">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 11&#93;</a></sup> In certain other cases, the extent of which varies from realm to realm, specific additional powers are reserved exclusively for the monarch\xe2\x80\x94such as the appointment of extra senators to the <a href="/wiki/Senate_of_Canada" title="Senate of Canada">Canadian Senate</a>, the creation of <a href="/wiki/Honour#Honours_and_awards" title="Honour">honours</a>, or the issuance of <a href="/wiki/Letters_patent" title="Letters patent">letters patent</a>\xe2\x80\x94and on occasions of national importance, the Queen may be advised to perform in person her constitutional duties, such as granting <a href="/wiki/Royal_Assent" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Assent">Royal Assent</a> or issuing a <a href="/wiki/Proclamation" title="Proclamation">royal proclamation</a>. Otherwise, all royal powers, including the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Prerogative" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Prerogative">Royal Prerogative</a>, are carried out on behalf of the sovereign by the relevant viceroy, who, apart from those already mentioned, include a <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant-Governor_(Canada)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lieutenant-Governor (Canada)">lieutenant governor</a> in each <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">province of Canada</a> (appointed by the <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>). In the United Kingdom, the Queen appoints <a href="/wiki/Counsellor_of_State" title="Counsellor of State">Counsellors of State</a> to perform her constitutional duties in her absence.\n</p><p>Similarly, the monarch will perform ceremonial duties in the Commonwealth realms to mark historically significant events.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> He or she does so most frequently in the United Kingdom and, in the other countries, during <a href="/wiki/List_of_Commonwealth_visits_made_by_Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Commonwealth visits made by Queen Elizabeth II">tours at least once every five or six years</a>, meaning the Queen is present in a number of her dominions outside the UK, or acting on behalf of those realms abroad, approximately every other year. For this work, the sovereign receives no salary from any state; instead, only the expenses incurred for each event (security, transportation, venue, etc.) are, due to the nature of the Crown in the realms, funded by the relevant state individually through the ordinary legislative budgeting process and, if called for, by the organisation that invited the sovereign\'s attendance. These engagements are organised in order for the Crown to honour, encourage, and learn about the achievements or endeavours of individuals, institutions, and enterprises in a variety of areas of the lives of the Queen\'s subjects.\n</p><p>Citizens in Commonwealth realms may request birthday or wedding anniversary messages to be sent from the sovereign. This is available for 100th, 105th, and beyond for birthdays; and 60th ("Diamond"), 65th, 70th ("Platinum"), and beyond for wedding anniversaries.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The monarch, in the form of the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> acts as the court of highest appeal in some but not all realms (and also, by agreement, for certain other former colonies which are not realms).\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religious_role_of_the_monarch">Religious role of the monarch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Religious role of the monarch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The sovereign\'s religious role differs from country to country. In all realms except Papua New Guinea, the Queen is sovereign "<a href="/wiki/By_the_Grace_of_God" title="By the Grace of God">by the Grace of God</a>", a phrase that forms a part of her official title within those states. In Canada, the United Kingdom, and New Zealand, "Defender of the Faith" (in Latin: <i><a href="/wiki/Fidei_defensor" class="mw-redirect" title="Fidei defensor">fidei defensor</a></i>)\xe2\x80\x94the ancient phrase first granted in 1521 by <a href="/wiki/Pope_Leo_X" title="Pope Leo X">Pope Leo X</a> to <a href="/wiki/King_Henry_VIII" class="mw-redirect" title="King Henry VIII">King Henry VIII</a>\xe2\x80\x94is also included as a part of the royal title and the sovereign is anointed as such in the only <a href="/wiki/Coronation" title="Coronation">coronation</a> that takes place in any of the realms,<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> a ceremony in the context of a church service imbued with theological and constitutional symbolism and meaning, held at <a href="/wiki/Westminster_Abbey" title="Westminster Abbey">Westminster Abbey</a> in <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>, United Kingdom.\n</p><p>However, it is solely in the United Kingdom that the Queen actually plays a role in organised religion. In <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>, she acts as the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Governor_of_the_Church_of_England" title="Supreme Governor of the Church of England">Supreme Governor of the Church of England</a> and appoints its bishops and archbishops who thereafter act as her <a href="/wiki/Lords_Spiritual" title="Lords Spiritual">Lords Spiritual</a>. In <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a>, she swears an oath to uphold and protect the <a href="/wiki/Church_of_Scotland" title="Church of Scotland">Church of Scotland</a> and sends to meetings of the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_the_Church_of_Scotland" title="General Assembly of the Church of Scotland">church\'s General Assembly</a> a <a href="/wiki/Lord_High_Commissioner" class="mw-redirect" title="Lord High Commissioner">Lord High Commissioner</a> as her representative, when she is not personally in attendance.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_family">Royal family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Royal family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<table class="vertical-navbox nowraplinks collapsible collapsed" style="float:right;clear:right;width:22.0em;margin:0 0 1.0em 1.0em;background:#f9f9f9;border:1px solid #aaa;padding:0.2em;border-spacing:0.4em Wales">HRH The Prince of Wales</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Camilla,_Duchess_of_Cornwall" title="Camilla, Duchess of Cornwall">HRH The Duchess of Cornwall</a>\n<ul><li><a
