href="/wiki/Prince_Harry,_Duke_of_Sussex" title="Prince Harry, Duke of Sussex">HRH The Duke of Sussex</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Meghan,_Duchess_of_Sussex" title="Meghan, Duchess of Sussex">HRH The Duchess of Sussex</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anne,_Princess_Royal" title="Anne, Princess Royal">HRH The Princess Royal</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Andrew,_Duke_of_York" title="Prince Andrew, Duke of York">HRH The Duke of York</a>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Beatrice_of_York" title="Princess Beatrice of York">HRH Princess Beatrice of York</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Eugenie_of_York" title="Princess Eugenie of York">HRH Princess Eugenie of York</a></li></ul></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Earl_of_Wessex" title="Prince Edward, Earl of Wessex">HRH The Earl of Wessex</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Sophie,_Countess_of_Wessex" title="Sophie, Countess of Wessex">HRH The Countess of Wessex</a></li></ul></li></ul>\n<hr />\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Richard,_Duke_of_Gloucester" title="Prince Richard, Duke of Gloucester">HRH The Duke of Gloucester</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Birgitte,_Duchess_of_Gloucester" title="Birgitte, Duchess of Gloucester">HRH The Duchess of Gloucester</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward,_Duke_of_Kent" title="Prince Edward, Duke of Kent">HRH The Duke of Kent</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Katharine,_Duchess_of_Kent" title="Katharine, Duchess of Kent">HRH The Duchess of Kent</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Princess_Alexandra,_The_Honourable_Lady_Ogilvy" title="Princess Alexandra, The Honourable Lady Ogilvy">HRH Princess Alexandra</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Prince_Michael_of_Kent" title="Prince Michael of Kent">HRH Prince Michael of Kent</a><br /><a href="/wiki/Princess_Michael_of_Kent" title="Princess Michael of Kent">HRH Princess Michael of Kent</a></li></ul></td>\n</tr><tr><td style="text-align:right;font-size:115%"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:British_Royal_Family" title="Template:British Royal Family"><abbr title="View this template">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:British_Royal_Family" title="Template talk:British Royal Family"><abbr title="Discuss this template">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:British_Royal_Family&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>There is no strict legal or formal definition of who is or is not a member of the royal family. The group is loosely defined as the extended family of the monarch who, either as representatives of the monarch or as part of their own charitable endeavours, perform public duties at events throughout the 16 realms each year. Events are funded in the same way as the monarch\'s ceremonial roles, and are formally recorded in the <a href="/wiki/Court_Circular" title="Court Circular">Court Circular</a>. Members of the royal family draw enormous media coverage in the form of photographic, written, and televised commentary on not only their activities and public roles, but also family relationships, <a href="/wiki/Rites_of_passage" class="mw-redirect" title="Rites of passage">rites of passage</a>, personalities, attire, and behaviour.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Flags">Flags</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Flags">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r856303569">@media all and (max-width:720px){.mw-parser-output .tmulti>.thumbinner{width:100%!important;max-width:none!important}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:none!important;width:100%!important;text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:204px;max-width:204px"><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William%2C_Duke_of_Cambridge.svg/200px-Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William%2C_Duke_of_Cambridge.svg.png" width="200" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William%2C_Duke_of_Cambridge.svg/300px-Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William%2C_Duke_of_Cambridge.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1b/Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William%2C_Duke_of_Cambridge.svg/400px-Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William%2C_Duke_of_Cambridge.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="500" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Royal Standard of <a href="/wiki/Prince_William,_Duke_of_Cambridge" title="Prince William, Duke of Cambridge">Prince William, Duke of Cambridge</a>, in the United Kingdom</div></div><div class="tsingle" style="margin:1px;width:202px;max-width:202px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William_(in_Canada).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William_%28in_Canada%29.svg/200px-Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William_%28in_Canada%29.svg.png" width="200" height="100" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William_%28in_Canada%29.svg/300px-Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William_%28in_Canada%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William_%28in_Canada%29.svg/400px-Royal_Standard_of_Prince_William_%28in_Canada%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="600" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption" style="clear:left">The Royal Standard of Prince William, Duke of Cambridge, in Canada<br />\n<hr /><br />\nSome members of the royal family have different <a href="/wiki/Heraldic_flag" title="Heraldic flag">heraldic standards</a> for use in the appropriate realm</div></div></div></div>\n<p>The Queen employs various <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Standard">royal standards</a> to mark her presence, the particular one used depending on which realm she is in or acting on behalf of at the time. There are currently unique flags for <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Australian_Flag" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Australian Flag">Australia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Barbadian_Flag" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Barbadian Flag">Barbados</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_standards_of_Canada" title="Royal standards of Canada">Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Jamaican_Flag" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Jamaican Flag">Jamaica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Personal_Flag_for_New_Zealand" title="Queen&#39;s Personal Flag for New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, and two variations for the United Kingdom\xe2\x80\x94one for <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_Scotland" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal Standard of Scotland">Scotland</a> and another for <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Royal Standard of the United Kingdom">the rest of the country</a>. All are <a href="/wiki/Heraldic_flag" title="Heraldic flag">heraldic banners</a> displaying the shield of the sovereign\'s <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> for that state, and each, save for those of the UK, are <a href="/wiki/Defacement_(flag)" title="Defacement (flag)">defaced</a> in the centre with the <a href="/wiki/Personal_Flag_of_Queen_Elizabeth_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Personal Flag of Queen Elizabeth II">Queen\'s Personal Flag</a>, a crowned <i>E</i> for <i>Elizabeth</i> surrounded by a garland of roses representing the countries of the Commonwealth. This latter flag on its own is used for realms that do not have a unique personal standard for the monarch, as well as for general use in representing the Queen as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">Head of the Commonwealth</a>. The monarch previously held royal standards for <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mauritius" title="Mauritius">Mauritius</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Trinidad_and_Tobago" title="Trinidad and Tobago">Trinidad and Tobago</a>, but these banners became obsolete when the countries became <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republics</a>.\n</p><p>Other members of the Royal Family have their own personal standards. In the United Kingdom, most have <a href="/wiki/Royal_Standard_of_the_United_Kingdom#Other_members_of_the_Royal_Family" title="Royal Standard of the United Kingdom">their own distinctive banner or banners</a>. The Prince of Wales, Duke of Cambridge, Princess Royal, Duke of York, and Earl of Wessex also have <a href="/wiki/Royal_standards_of_Canada#Other_members_of_the_Royal_Family" title="Royal standards of Canada">one each for Canada</a>, and the remaining members of the Royal Family use a specific ermine-bordered banner of the Canadian royal arms. Those who do not possess a standard for an individual realm other than the UK will use their British standard to identify themselves when touring other Commonwealth realms and foreign countries.\n</p><p>The governors-general throughout the Commonwealth realms also each use a personal flag, which, like that of the sovereign, passes to each successive occupant of the office. Most feature a <a href="/wiki/Lions_passant" class="mw-redirect" title="Lions passant">lion passant</a> atop a <a href="/wiki/St._Edward%27s_Crown" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Edward&#39;s Crown">St. Edward\'s</a> <a href="/wiki/Crown_(heraldry)#Commonwealth_usage" title="Crown (heraldry)">royal crown</a> with the name of the country across a scroll underneath, all on a blue background. The two exceptions are those of, since 1981, <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Flag of the Governor General of Canada">Canada</a> (bearing on a blue background the <a href="/wiki/Crest_(heraldry)" title="Crest (heraldry)">crest</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Arms_of_Canada" title="Arms of Canada">Royal Coat of Arms of Canada</a>) and, since 2008, <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_the_Governor-General_of_New_Zealand" title="Flag of the Governor-General of New Zealand">New Zealand</a> (a St. Edward\'s Crown above the <a href="/wiki/Escutcheon_(heraldry)" title="Escutcheon (heraldry)">shield</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms_of_New_Zealand" title="Coat of arms of New Zealand">Coat of Arms of New Zealand</a>). The lieutenant governors of the Canadian provinces each have <a href="/wiki/Flags_of_the_Lieutenant-Governors_of_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Flags of the Lieutenant-Governors of Canada">their own personal standards</a>, as <a href="/wiki/Flags_of_the_Governors_of_the_Australian_states" title="Flags of the Governors of the Australian states">do the governors of the Australian states</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_development">Historical development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Historical development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dominions_emerge">Dominions emerge</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Dominions emerge">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The possibility that a colony within the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> might become a new kingdom was first mooted in the 1860s, when it was proposed that the <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North American</a> territories of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a> unite as a <a href="/wiki/Confederation" title="Confederation">confederation</a> that might be known as the <i>Kingdom of Canada</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> In light of geo-political circumstances at the time, however, the name was abandoned in favour of the <i><a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Dominion of Canada</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-Dom_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dom-87">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 12&#93;</a></sup> As more British colonies followed Canada in gaining legislative independence from the United Kingdom, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a> Sir <a href="/wiki/Wilfrid_Laurier" title="Wilfrid Laurier">Wilfrid Laurier</a> insisted at the 1907 <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Conference" title="Imperial Conference">Imperial Conference</a> that a formula be created to differentiate between the Crown and the <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing colonies</a>. For the latter the Canadian precedent was followed, and the term <i><a href="/wiki/Dominion" title="Dominion">Dominion</a></i> was extended to apply to Australia, New Zealand, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, and the colonies of <a href="/wiki/Cape_Colony" title="Cape Colony">the Cape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Natal" title="Colony of Natal">Natal</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transvaal_Colony" title="Transvaal Colony">Transvaal</a>, before and after they merged in 1910 with the <a href="/wiki/Orange_River_Colony" title="Orange River Colony">Orange River Colony</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a>. These countries were joined by the <a href="/wiki/Irish_Free_State" title="Irish Free State">Irish Free State</a> in December 1922, as part of the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Irish_Treaty" title="Anglo-Irish Treaty">Anglo-Irish Treaty</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg/220px-William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg" width="220" height="263" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg/330px-William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg/440px-William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2271" data-file-height="2720" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:William_Orpen_-_The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/William_Orpen" title="William Orpen">William Orpen</a>\'s <i><a href="/wiki/The_Signing_of_Peace_in_the_Hall_of_Mirrors" title="The Signing of Peace in the Hall of Mirrors">The Signing of Peace in the Hall of Mirrors</a></i>: a compiled portrait of the main delegates to the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, including some of the Dominion delegates<sup id="cite_ref-Image2a_88-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Image2a-88">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 13&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ImperialConference.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/220px-ImperialConference.jpg" width="220" height="174" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/330px-ImperialConference.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/ImperialConference.jpg/440px-ImperialConference.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="507" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ImperialConference.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King <a href="/wiki/George_V" title="George V">George V</a> with his prime ministers at the <a href="/wiki/1926_Imperial_Conference" title="1926 Imperial Conference">Imperial Conference of 1926</a><sup id="cite_ref-Image3_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Image3-89">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 14&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Although the Dominions were capable of governing themselves internally, they technically remained\xe2\x80\x94especially in regard to foreign policy and defence\xe2\x80\x94subject to British authority, wherein the <a href="/wiki/Governor-General" class="mw-redirect" title="Governor-General">governor-general</a> of each Dominion represented the <a href="/wiki/British_monarch" class="mw-redirect" title="British monarch">British monarch</a>-<a href="/wiki/Queen-in-Council" class="mw-redirect" title="Queen-in-Council">in-Council</a> reigning over these territories as a single <a href="/wiki/Empire" title="Empire">imperial</a> domain. It was commonly held in some circles that the Crown was a monolithic element throughout all the monarch\'s territories; A.H. Lefroy wrote in 1918 that "the Crown is to be considered as one and indivisible throughout the Empire; and cannot be severed into as many kingships as there are Dominions, and self-governing colonies."<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> This unitary model began to erode, however, when the Dominions gained more international prominence as a result of their participation and sacrifice in the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, in 1919 prompting Canadian prime minister Sir <a href="/wiki/Robert_Borden" title="Robert Borden">Robert Borden</a> and South African minister of defence <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smuts" title="Jan Smuts">Jan Smuts</a> to demand that the Dominions be given at the <a href="/wiki/Paris_Peace_Conference,_1919" title="Paris Peace Conference, 1919">Versailles Conference</a> full recognition as "autonomous nations of an Imperial Commonwealth." The immediate result was that, though the King signed as High Contracting Party for the empire as a whole,<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> the Dominions were also separate signatories to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, as well as, together with <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>, founding members of the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>. In 1921 the Prime Minister of the United Kingdom <a href="/wiki/David_Lloyd_George" title="David Lloyd George">David Lloyd George</a> stated that the "British Dominions have now been accepted fully into the community of nations."<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Interwar_period">Interwar period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Interwar period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The pace of independence increased in the 1920s, led by Canada, which exchanged envoys with the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a> in 1920 and concluded the <a href="/wiki/Halibut_Treaty" title="Halibut Treaty">Halibut Fisheries Treaty</a> in its own right in 1923.<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> In the <a href="/wiki/Chanak_crisis" class="mw-redirect" title="Chanak crisis">Chanak crisis</a> of 1922, the Canadian government insisted that its course of action would be determined by the Canadian parliament,<sup id="cite_ref-Buckner2008_93-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Buckner2008-93">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> not the British government, and, by 1925, the Dominions felt confident enough to refuse to be bound by Britain\'s adherence to the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Locarno" class="mw-redirect" title="Treaty of Locarno">Treaty of Locarno</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Hilliker1990_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Hilliker1990-94">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> These developments, combined with a realisation that the Crown was already operating distinctly and separately within each of the jurisdictions of the Canadian provinces and Australian states,<sup id="cite_ref-Haldane_96-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Haldane-96">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 15&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> appeared to put to rest previous assertions that the Crown could never be divided amongst the Dominions.\n</p><p>Another catalyst for change came in 1926, when <a href="/wiki/Field_Marshal_(United_Kingdom)" class="mw-redirect" title="Field Marshal (United Kingdom)">Field Marshal</a> <a href="/wiki/Julian_Byng,_1st_Viscount_Byng_of_Vimy" title="Julian Byng, 1st Viscount Byng of Vimy">the Lord Byng of Vimy</a>, then <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>, refused the advice of his prime minister (<a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a>) in what came to be known colloquially as the <a href="/wiki/King%E2%80%93Byng_Affair" class="mw-redirect" title="King\xe2\x80\x93Byng Affair">King\xe2\x80\x93Byng Affair</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup> Mackenzie King, after resigning and then being reappointed as prime minister some months later, pushed at the <a href="/wiki/1926_Imperial_Conference" title="1926 Imperial Conference">Imperial Conference of 1926</a> for a reorganisation of the way the Dominions related to the British government, resulting in the <a href="/wiki/Balfour_Declaration_of_1926" title="Balfour Declaration of 1926">Balfour Declaration</a>, which declared formally that the Dominions were fully autonomous and equal in status to the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> What this meant in practice was not at the time worked out; conflicting views existed, some in the United Kingdom not wishing to see a fracturing of the sacred unity of the Crown throughout the empire, and some in the Dominions not wishing to see their jurisdiction have to take on the full brunt of diplomatic and military responsibilities.<sup id="cite_ref-Mallory_36-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Mallory-36">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>What did follow was that the Dominion governments gained an equal status with the United Kingdom, a separate and direct relationship with the monarch, without the British Cabinet acting as an intermediary, and the governors-general now acted solely as a personal representative of the sovereign in right of that Dominion.<sup id="cite_ref-Balf_101-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Balf-101">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup> Though no formal mechanism for tendering advice to the monarch had yet been established\xe2\x80\x94former <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Prime Minister of Australia</a> <a href="/wiki/Billy_Hughes" title="Billy Hughes">William Morris Hughes</a> theorised that the Dominion cabinets would provide informal direction and the British Cabinet would offer formal advice<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>\xe2\x80\x94the concepts were first put into legal practice with the passage in 1927 of the <a href="/wiki/Royal_and_Parliamentary_Titles_Act_1927" title="Royal and Parliamentary Titles Act 1927">Royal and Parliamentary Titles Act</a>, which implicitly recognised the Irish Free State as separate from the UK, and the King as king <i>of</i> each Dominion uniquely, rather than as the British king <i>in</i> each Dominion. At the same time, terminology in foreign relations was altered to demonstrate the independent status of the Dominions, such as the dropping of the term "Britannic" from the King\'s style outside of the United Kingdom.<sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Then, in 1930 George V\'s <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Australia" title="Cabinet of Australia">Australian ministers</a> employed a practice adopted by resolution at that year\'s Imperial Conference,<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> directly advising the King to appoint Sir <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Isaacs" title="Isaac Isaacs">Isaac Isaacs</a> as his <a href="/wiki/Governor-General_of_Australia" title="Governor-General of Australia">Australian governor-general</a>, against the preferences of the British government and the King himself.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Statute_of_Westminster">Statute of Westminster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Statute of Westminster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a></div>\n<p>These new developments were explicitly codified in 1931 with the passage of the Statute of Westminster, through which Canada, the Union of South Africa, and the Irish Free State all immediately obtained formal legislative independence from the UK, while in the other Dominions adoption of the statute was subject to ratification by the Dominion\'s parliament. Australia and New Zealand did so in 1942 and 1947, respectively, with the former\'s ratification back-dated to 1939, while Newfoundland never ratified the bill and reverted to direct British rule in 1934. As a result, the <a href="/wiki/Parliament_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Parliament of the United Kingdom">parliament at Westminster</a> was unable to legislate for any Dominion unless requested to do so,<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> although the <a href="/wiki/Judicial_Committee_of_the_Privy_Council" title="Judicial Committee of the Privy Council">Judicial Committee of the Privy Council</a> was left available as the last court of appeal for some Dominions.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> Specific attention was given in the statute\'s preamble to royal succession, outlining that no changes to that line could be made by the parliament of the United Kingdom or that of any Dominion without the assent of all the other parliaments of the UK and Dominions, an arrangement a justice of the Ontario Superior Court in 2003 likened to "a treaty among the Commonwealth countries to share the monarchy under the existing rules and not to change the rules without the agreement of all signatories."<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia,_1936.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1936.jpg/220px-King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1936.jpg" width="220" height="292" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1936.jpg/330px-King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1936.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1936.jpg/440px-King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia%2C_1936.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1509" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:King_Edward_VIII_and_Mrs_Simpson_on_holiday_in_Yugoslavia,_1936.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>King Edward VIII and Wallis Simpson on holiday in the Mediterranean, 1936</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg/220px-CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg" width="220" height="162" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg/330px-CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/27/CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg/440px-CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="470" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CommonwealthPrimeMinisters1944.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The prime ministers of five Commonwealth countries at the 1944 <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Heads_of_Government_Meeting" title="Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting">Commonwealth Prime Ministers\' Conference</a>; from left to right: <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a> (Canada), <a href="/wiki/Jan_Smuts" title="Jan Smuts">Jan Smuts</a> (South Africa), <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> (United Kingdom), <a href="/wiki/Peter_Fraser" title="Peter Fraser">Peter Fraser</a> (New Zealand), and <a href="/wiki/John_Curtin" title="John Curtin">John Curtin</a> (Australia)</div></div></div>\n<p>This was all met with only minor trepidation, either before or at the time,<sup id="cite_ref-Anti_108-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Anti-108">&#91;\xe2\x80\xa0 17&#93;</a></sup> and the government of Ireland was confident that the relationship of these independent countries under the Crown would function as a <a href="/wiki/Personal_union" title="Personal union">personal union</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-murdoch1_25-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-murdoch1-25">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup> akin to that which had earlier existed between the United Kingdom and <a href="/wiki/Hanover" title="Hanover">Hanover</a> (1801 to 1837), or between <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a> and <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scotland</a> (1603 to 1707). Its first test came, though, with the <a href="/wiki/Edward_VIII_abdication_crisis" title="Edward VIII abdication crisis">abdication of King Edward VIII</a> in 1936,<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> for which it was necessary to gain the consent of the governments of all the Dominions and the request and consent of the Canadian government, as well as separate legislation in South Africa and the Irish Free State, before the resignation could take place across the Commonwealth.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The civil division of the <a href="/wiki/Court_of_Appeal_of_England_and_Wales" class="mw-redirect" title="Court of Appeal of England and Wales">Court of Appeal of England and Wales</a> later found in 1982 that the British parliament could have legislated for a Dominion simply by including in any new law a clause claiming the Dominion cabinet had requested and approved of the act, whether that was true or not.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup> Further, the British parliament was not obliged to fulfil a Dominion\'s request for legislative change. Regardless, in 1935 the British parliament refused to consider the result of the <a href="/wiki/Secessionism_in_Western_Australia#1933_referendum" title="Secessionism in Western Australia">Western Australian secession referendum of 1933</a> without the approval of the Australian federal parliament. In 1937, the Appeal Division of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_South_Africa" title="Supreme Court of South Africa">Supreme Court of South Africa</a> ruled unanimously that a repeal of the Statute of Westminster in the United Kingdom would have no effect in South Africa, stating: "We cannot take this argument seriously. Freedom once conferred cannot be revoked."<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> Others in Canada upheld the same position.<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Independent_Dominions">Independent Dominions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Independent Dominions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>At the 1932 <a href="/wiki/British_Empire_Economic_Conference" title="British Empire Economic Conference">British Empire Economic Conference</a>, delegates from the United Kingdom, led by <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baldwin" title="Stanley Baldwin">Stanley Baldwin</a> (then <a href="/wiki/Lord_President_of_the_Council" title="Lord President of the Council">Lord President of the Council</a>),<sup id="cite_ref-Kaufman976_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaufman976-112">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> hoped to establish a system of <a href="/wiki/Free_trade" title="Free trade">free trade</a> within the British Commonwealth, to promote unity within the British Empire and to assure Britain\'s position as a world power. The idea was controversial, as it pitted proponents of imperial trade with those who sought a general policy of trade liberalisation with all nations. The Dominions, particularly Canada, were also adamantly against dispensing with their import tariffs,<sup id="cite_ref-NA_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NA-113">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> which "dispelled any romantic notions of a \'United Empire\'."<sup id="cite_ref-Kaufman976_112-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kaufman976-112">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The meeting, however, did produce a five year <a href="/wiki/Trade_agreement" title="Trade agreement">trade agreement</a> based upon a policy, first conceived in the 1900s,<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> of <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Preference" title="Imperial Preference">Imperial Preference</a>: the countries retained their import tariffs, but lowered these for other Commonwealth countries.<sup id="cite_ref-NA_113-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NA-113">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During his tenure as Governor General of Canada, <a href="/wiki/John_Buchan,_1st_Baron_Tweedsmuir" class="mw-redirect" title="John Buchan, 1st Baron Tweedsmuir">Lord Tweedsmuir</a> urged the organisation of <a href="/wiki/1939_royal_tour_of_Canada" title="1939 royal tour of Canada">a royal tour</a> of the country by King George VI, so that he might not only appear in person before his people, but also personally perform constitutional duties and pay a <a href="/wiki/State_visit" title="State visit">state visit</a> to the United States as <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Canada" title="Monarchy of Canada">king of Canada</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-LAC_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAC-116">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> While the idea was embraced in Canada as a way to "translate the Statute of Westminster into the actualities of a tour," throughout the planning of the trip that took place in 1939, the British authorities resisted at numerous points the idea that the King be attended by his Canadian ministers instead of his British ones.<sup id="cite_ref-Parl_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Parl-117">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup> The Canadian prime minister (still Mackenzie King) was ultimately successful, however, in being the minister in attendance, and the King did in public throughout the trip ultimately act solely in his capacity as the Canadian monarch. The status of the Crown was bolstered by Canada\'s reception of George VI.<sup id="cite_ref-LAC_116-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LAC-116">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>When <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a> began, there was some uncertainty in the Dominions about the ramifications of Britain\'s declaration of war against <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>. Australia and New Zealand had not yet ratified the Statute of Westminster; the Australian prime minister, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Menzies" title="Robert Menzies">Robert Menzies</a>, considered the government bound by the British declaration of war,<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Boyce27_120-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyce27-120">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> while New Zealand coordinated a declaration of war to be made simultaneously with Britain\'s.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> As late as 1937, some scholars were still of the mind that, when it came to declarations of war, if the King signed, he did so as king of the empire as a whole; at that time, W. Kennedy wrote: "in the final test of sovereignty\xe2\x80\x94that of war\xe2\x80\x94Canada is not a sovereign state... and it remains as true in 1937 as it was in 1914 that when the Crown is at war, Canada is legally at war,"<sup id="cite_ref-Kennedy1938_122-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kennedy1938-122">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> and, one year later, <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Berriedale_Keith" title="Arthur Berriedale Keith">Arthur Berriedale Keith</a> argued that "issues of war or neutrality still are decided on the final authority of the British Cabinet."<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> In 1939, however, Canada and South Africa made separate proclamations of war against Germany a few days after the UK\'s. Their example was followed more consistently by the other realms as further war was declared against <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hungary" title="Hungary">Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Heard_91-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heard-91">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/%C3%89ire" title="\xc3\x89ire">\xc3\x89ire</a> (the independent Irish state) remained neutral.<sup id="cite_ref-Boyce27_120-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Boyce27-120">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> At the war\'s end, it was said by F.R. Scott that "it is firmly established as a basic constitutional principle that, so far as relates to Canada, the King is regulated by Canadian law and must act only on the advice and responsibility of Canadian ministers."<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-war_evolution">Post-war evolution</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Post-war evolution">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Within three years following the end of the Second World War, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_India" title="Dominion of India">India</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan" title="Dominion of Pakistan">Pakistan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Ceylon" title="Dominion of Ceylon">Ceylon</a> became independent realms within the Commonwealth (then still called <i>Dominions</i>), though it was made clear at the time that India would soon move to a republican form of government. Unlike the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Ireland" title="Republic of Ireland">Republic of Ireland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Burma" class="mw-redirect" title="Burma">Burma</a> at the time of their becoming republics, however, there was no desire on the part of India to give up its membership in the British Commonwealth, prompting a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Heads_of_Government_Meeting" title="Commonwealth Heads of Government Meeting">Commonwealth Conference</a> and the issuance of the <a href="/wiki/London_Declaration" title="London Declaration">London Declaration</a> in April 1949, which entrenched the idea of Canadian prime minister <a href="/wiki/Louis_St._Laurent" title="Louis St. Laurent">Louis St. Laurent</a> that different <a href="/wiki/Royal_house" class="mw-redirect" title="Royal house">royal houses</a> and <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republics</a> be allowed in the Commonwealth so long as they recognised as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_the_Commonwealth" title="Head of the Commonwealth">the international organisation\'s symbolic head</a> the shared sovereign of the United Kingdom and the Dominions.<sup id="cite_ref-Smith_125-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Smith-125">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup> Shortly before the London Declaration, <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a>, which had remained a Dominion in name only, had become a province of Canada.\n</p><p>At approximately the same time, the tabling in 1946 of the Canadian parliament\'s Canadian Citizenship Act had brought into question the homogeneity of the King\'s subjects, which, prior to that year, was uniformly defined in terms of allegiance to the sovereign, without regard to the individual\'s country of residence. Following negotiations, it was decided in 1947 that each Commonwealth member was free to pass its own citizenship legislation, so that its citizens owed allegiance only to the monarch in right of that country.\n</p><p>As these constitutional developments were taking place, the Dominion and British governments became increasingly concerned with how to represent the more commonly accepted notion that there was no distinction between the sovereign\'s role in the United Kingdom and his or her position in any of the Dominions. Thus, at the 1948 Prime Ministers\' Conference the term <i>Dominion</i> was avoided in favour of <i>Commonwealth country</i>, in order to avoid the subordination implied by the older designation.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="From_the_accession_of_Queen_Elizabeth_II">From the accession of Queen Elizabeth II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: From the accession of Queen Elizabeth II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>With the British <a href="/wiki/Proclamation_of_accession_of_Elizabeth_II" title="Proclamation of accession of Elizabeth II">proclamation of Elizabeth II\'s accession</a> to the throne in 1952, the phrases <i>Commonwealth realm</i> and <i>Head of the Commonwealth</i> became established, deriving from the words that declared the monarch as "of this Realm, and of her other Realms and Territories Queen, Head of the Commonwealth." Previously, the term <i>realm</i> in its singular form was understood to refer to the entire British Empire, rather than a "separate kingdom" under a shared crown.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG/220px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG" width="220" height="327" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG/330px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG/440px-Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="949" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Queen_Elizabeth_II_-_1953-Dress.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a> in 1953</div></div></div>\n<p>The Commonwealth realms\' prime ministers thereafter discussed the matter of the new monarch\'s title, with St. Laurent stating at the 1953 Commonwealth Conference that it was important to agree on a format that would "emphasise the fact that the Queen is Queen of Canada, regardless of her sovereignty over other Commonwealth countries."<sup id="cite_ref-HCUK_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HCUK-57">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> The result was a new <a href="/wiki/Royal_Style_and_Titles_Act" title="Royal Style and Titles Act">Royal Style and Titles Act</a> being passed in each of the seven realms then existing (excluding <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Pakistan" title="Dominion of Pakistan">Pakistan</a>), which all identically gave formal recognition to the separateness and equality of the countries involved, and replaced the phrase "British Dominions Beyond the Seas" with "Her Other Realms and Territories", the latter using the medieval <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a> word <i>realm</i> (from <i>royaume</i>) in place of <i>dominion</i>. Further, at her coronation, Elizabeth II\'s oath contained a provision requiring her to promise to govern according to the rules and customs of the realms, naming each one separately. The change in perspective was summed up by <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Gordon_Walker" title="Patrick Gordon Walker">Patrick Gordon Walker</a>\'s statement in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">British House of Commons</a>: "We in this country have to abandon... any sense of property in the Crown. The Queen, now, clearly, explicitly and according to title, belongs equally to all her realms and to the Commonwealth as a whole."<sup id="cite_ref-Bogdanor_56-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bogdanor-56">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the same period, Walker also suggested to the British parliament that the Queen should annually spend an equal amount of time in each of her realms. <a href="/wiki/John_Grigg,_2nd_Baron_Altrincham" title="John Grigg, 2nd Baron Altrincham">Lord Altrincham</a>, who in 1957 criticised Queen Elizabeth II for having a <a href="/wiki/Court_(royal)" class="mw-redirect" title="Court (royal)">court</a> that encompassed mostly Britain and not the Commonwealth as a whole,<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> was in favour of the idea, but it did not attract wide support.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> Another thought raised was that viceregal appointments should become trans-Commonwealth; the Governor-General of Australia would be someone from South Africa, the Governor-General of Ceylon would come from New Zealand, and so on. The prime ministers of Canada and Australia, <a href="/wiki/John_Diefenbaker" title="John Diefenbaker">John Diefenbaker</a> and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Menzies" title="Robert Menzies">Robert Menzies</a>, respectively, were sympathetic to the concept, but, again, it was never put into practice.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 6 July 2010, Queen Elizabeth II addressed the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> in <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> as queen of all 16 Commonwealth realms.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> The following year, <a href="/wiki/Portia_Simpson-Miller" title="Portia Simpson-Miller">Portia Simpson-Miller</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Jamaica" title="Prime Minister of Jamaica">Prime Minister of Jamaica</a>, spoke of a desire to make that country a republic,<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Alex_Salmond" title="Alex Salmond">Alex Salmond</a>, the <a href="/wiki/First_Minister_of_Scotland" title="First Minister of Scotland">First Minister of Scotland</a> and leader of the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_National_Party" title="Scottish National Party">Scottish National Party</a> (which favours <a href="/wiki/Scottish_independence" title="Scottish independence">Scottish independence</a>), stated an independent Scotland "would still share a monarchy with... the UK, just as... 16 [sic] other Commonwealth countries do now."<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Dennis_Canavan" title="Dennis Canavan">Dennis Canavan</a>, leader of <a href="/wiki/Yes_Scotland" title="Yes Scotland">Yes Scotland</a>, disagreed and said a separate, post-independence referendum should be held on the matter.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the <a href="/wiki/Perth_Agreement" title="Perth Agreement">Perth Agreement</a> of 2011, the Commonwealth realms, in accordance with convention, together engaged in a process of amending the common line of succession according to each country\'s constitution, to ensure the order would continue to be identical in every realm. In legislative debates in the United Kingdom, the term <i>Commonwealth realm</i> was employed.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Former_Commonwealth_realms">Former Commonwealth realms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Former Commonwealth realms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="List_of_states">List of states</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-references-wrap"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-138"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-138">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The flags shown are the national flags of each country at the time it became a Commonwealth realm.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-139"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-139">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Renamed <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">Sri Lanka</a> upon becoming a republic. The <a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Sri_Lanka" title="Flag of Sri Lanka">Ceylonese flag</a> changed in 1951.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Dominion-140"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Dominion_140-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Dominion_140-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text">Part of the group of independent countries within the British Commonwealth of Nations that shared the same person as their reigning monarch, but only ever designated as <i>Dominions</i>, each becoming a republic or joining another sovereign state before the term <i>Commonwealth realms</i> began to be used.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-141"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-141">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See also: <a href="/wiki/Irish_head_of_state_from_1936_to_1949" class="mw-redirect" title="Irish head of state from 1936 to 1949">Irish head of state from 1936 to 1949</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-142"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-142">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Now a part of <a href="/wiki/Tanzania" title="Tanzania">Tanzania</a>.</span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<p>In addition to the states listed above, the <a href="/wiki/Dominion_of_Newfoundland" title="Dominion of Newfoundland">Dominion of Newfoundland</a> was a dominion when the <a href="/wiki/Statute_of_Westminster_1931" title="Statute of Westminster 1931">Statute of Westminster 1931</a> was given royal assent but effectively lost that status in 1934, without ever have assented to the Statute of Westminster, and before the term Commonwealth realm ever came into use. Due to a domestic financial and political crisis, the <a href="/wiki/General_Assembly_of_Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="General Assembly of Newfoundland and Labrador">Newfoundland legislature</a> petitioned the UK to suspend Dominion status,  the UK parliament passed the <i>Newfoundland Act 1933</i>, and <a href="/wiki/Commission_of_Government" class="mw-redirect" title="Commission of Government">direct rule</a> was implemented in 1934. Rather than reclaiming dominion status after World War II, it became a province of Canada in 1949.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Republican_referendums">Republican referendums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Republican referendums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>A number of Commonwealth realms have held referendums to consider whether they should become republics. As of January 2017, of the eight referendums held, only three have been successful: in <a href="/wiki/Ghana" title="Ghana">Ghana</a>, in <a href="/wiki/South_Africa" title="South Africa">South Africa</a> and the second referendum in <a href="/wiki/Gambia" class="mw-redirect" title="Gambia">Gambia</a>. Referendums which rejected the proposal were held in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a>, twice in <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Saint_Vincent_and_the_Grenadines" title="Saint Vincent and the Grenadines">Saint Vincent and the Grenadines</a>. There are currently no planned referendums, but interest in holding a second referendum was expressed in <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> in 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable" style="text-align:right">\n\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year therefore the proposal was rejected.</li></ol>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul style="display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold">\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Commonwealth_Realms_map2.png" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Commonwealth_Realms_map2.png/32px-Commonwealth_Realms_map2.png" width="32" height="15" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Commonwealth_Realms_map2.png/48px-Commonwealth_Realms_map2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7e/Commonwealth_Realms_map2.png/64px-Commonwealth_Realms_map2.png 2x" data-file-width="1357" data-file-height="628" /></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Commonwealth_realms" title="Portal:Commonwealth realms">Commonwealth realms portal</a></span></li>\n<li style="display:table-row"><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center"><a href="/wiki/File:Crown_of_Saint_Edward_Heraldry.svg" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Crown_of_Saint_Edward_Heraldry.svg/30px-Crown_of_Saint_Edward_Heraldry.svg.png" width="30" height="28" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Crown_of_Saint_Edward_Heraldry.svg/45px-Crown_of_Saint_Edward_Heraldry.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Crown_of_Saint_Edward_Heraldry.svg/60px-Crown_of_Saint_Edward_Heraldry.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="115" data-file-height="108" /></a></span><span style="display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle"><a href="/wiki/Portal:Monarchy" title="Portal:Monarchy">Monarchy portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Family" title="Commonwealth Family">Commonwealth Family</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Imperial_Federation" title="Imperial Federation">Imperial Federation</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Member states of the Commonwealth of Nations">Member states of the Commonwealth of Nations</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/States_headed_by_Elizabeth_II" title="States headed by Elizabeth II">States headed by Elizabeth II</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Union_of_the_Crowns" title="Union of the Crowns">Union of the Crowns</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Notes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Together with <a href="/wiki/Associated_state" title="Associated state">associated states</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dependent_territory" title="Dependent territory">dependencies</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Scott1-24"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Scott1_24-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">F.R. Scott stated: "The common kinship within the British group today establishes a form of personal union, the members of which are legally capable of following different international policies even in time of war."<sup id="cite_ref-scott1_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scott1-23">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Elliott1-29"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Elliott1_29-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">W.Y Elliott stated: If a personal union be chosen, the Crown will be forced to act on the king\'s own discretion [and] since personal discretion is a modern monarch is unthinkable, the only alternative would be a league of states with a common but symbolic crown",<sup id="cite_ref-elliott1_27-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elliott1-27">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> and Alexander N. Sack stated: "Whatever the future development of the British Commonwealth may be [it] can be described as a that of associations or unions of States, as distinguished from \'personal\' unions, on the one hand, and federal States, on the other.<sup id="cite_ref-sack1_28-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-sack1-28">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Miller1-32"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Miller1_32-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">J. D. B. Miller stated:[T]he survey concludes with an attempt to classify the Commonwealth. It is no longer a federation, nor a military alliance, nor a personal union.<sup id="cite_ref-miller1_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-miller1-31">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Conf-45"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Conf_45-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">During a British <a href="/wiki/State_visit" title="State visit">state visit</a> to <a href="/wiki/Jordan" title="Jordan">Jordan</a> in 1984, Queen Elizabeth II made a speech expressing opinions of her <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Cabinet of the United Kingdom">British Cabinet</a> that countered the views of her <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Australia" title="Cabinet of Australia">Australian Cabinet</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> though the Queen was evidently not representing Australia at that time. Similarly, Elizabeth II undertook a visit to <a href="/wiki/Latin_America" title="Latin America">Latin America</a> to promote British goods at the same time a Canadian ministerial trip was underway in the same region in order to promote Canadian products.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-War-46"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-War_46-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">On 3 September 1939, the United Kingdom declared war on <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>, but it was only on 6 September that, under the articles of the Statute of Westminster, the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_South_Africa" title="Union of South Africa">Union of South Africa</a> did same, followed by Canada on 10 September. Therefore, from 3 to 10 September, King <a href="/wiki/George_VI" title="George VI">George VI</a>, as king of the United Kingdom, South Africa and Canada, was both at war and at peace with Germany. Similarly, as he was still technically <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_Ireland" title="Monarchy of Ireland">monarch of Ireland</a>, it was George VI\'s duty to validate the credentials of the <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany#Foreign_relations" title="Nazi Germany">German</a> <a href="/wiki/Consul_(representative)" title="Consul (representative)">consul</a> to Ireland, which remained <a href="/wiki/Irish_neutrality_during_World_War_II" title="Irish neutrality during World War II">neutral</a> throughout <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">the war</a>.<br />A more extreme example was the <a href="/wiki/Indo-Pakistani_War_of_1947" class="mw-redirect" title="Indo-Pakistani War of 1947">Indo-Pakistani War of 1947</a>, in which George VI, as head of state of both warring nations, was, in a legal sense, at war with himself. Similarly, in 1983 Queen Elizabeth II was monarch of <a href="/wiki/Grenada" title="Grenada">Grenada</a> when <a href="/wiki/List_of_Governors-General_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="List of Governors-General of Grenada">her governor-general there</a> requested the <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Grenada" class="mw-redirect" title="Invasion of Grenada">invasion of the country</a> by a number of other <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> states, including some that were also realms of the Queen; an undertaking that was opposed by a number of Elizabeth\'s other governments, such as those of the United Kingdom, Canada, and <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">Belize</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-GGs-47"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-GGs_47-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the example of the 1983 invasion of Grenada, the Governor-General, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Scoon" title="Paul Scoon">Sir Paul Scoon</a>, invited the intervention of foreign troops deliberately without ever having informed the Queen. Also, when <a href="/wiki/John_Kerr_(Governor-General)" class="mw-redirect" title="John Kerr (Governor-General)">Sir John Kerr</a> <a href="/wiki/Australian_constitutional_crisis_of_1975" class="mw-redirect" title="Australian constitutional crisis of 1975">dismissed the Australian government</a> in 1975, he did not inform the Queen of his intent to do so.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Toporoski-60"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Toporoski_60-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">One Canadian constitutional scholar, Dr. Richard Toporoski, stated on this: "I am perfectly prepared to concede, even happily affirm, that the British Crown no longer exists in Canada, but that is because legal reality indicates to me that in one sense, the British Crown no longer exists in Britain: the Crown transcends Britain just as much as it does Canada. One can therefore speak of \'the British Crown\' or \'the Canadian Crown\' or indeed the \'Barbadian\' or \'Tuvaluan\' Crown, but what one will mean by the term is the Crown acting or expressing itself within the context of that particular jurisdiction".<sup id="cite_ref-Toporoski_59-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Toporoski-59">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-SueHill-62"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-SueHill_62-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">See <a href="/wiki/Sue_v_Hill" title="Sue v Hill">Sue v Hill</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Cox-74"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Cox_74-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Noel Cox stated: "Any alteration by the United Kingdom Parliament in the law touching the succession to the throne would, except perhaps in the case of Papua New Guinea, be ineffective to alter the succession to the throne in respect of, and in accordance with the law of, any other independent member of the Commonwealth which was within the Queen\'s realms at the time of such alteration. Therefore it is more than mere constitutional convention that requires that the assent of the Parliament of each member of the Commonwealth within the Queen\'s realms be obtained in respect of any such alteration in the law."<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n\nRichard Toporoski similarly stated: "[I]f, let us say, an alteration were to be made in the United Kingdom to the Act of Settlement 1701, providing for the succession of the Crown. It is my opinion that the domestic constitutional law of Australia or Papua New Guinea, for example, would provide for the succession in those countries of the same person who became Sovereign of the United Kingdom ... If the British law were to be changed and we [Canada] did not change our law ... the Crown would be divided. The person provided for in the new law would become king or queen in at least some realms of the Commonwealth; Canada would continue on with the person who would have become monarch under the previous law ...<sup id="cite_ref-Topo_73-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Topo-73">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Viceroy-79"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Viceroy_79-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">In the <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Islands" title="Solomon Islands">Solomon Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuvalu" title="Tuvalu">Tuvalu</a>, the prime minister must consult the legislature in confidence; in <a href="/wiki/Papua_New_Guinea" title="Papua New Guinea">Papua New Guinea</a>, the governor-general is nominated to the Queen by a parliamentary vote.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Dom-87"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Dom_87-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The <a href="/wiki/Colonial_Office" title="Colonial Office">Colonial Office</a> in London opposed this potentially "premature" and "pretentious" reference for a new country, and were also wary of antagonising the <a href="/wiki/United_States" title="United States">United States</a>, which had emerged from its <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">Civil War</a> as a formidable military power with unsettled grievances because of British support for the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">Confederate</a> cause. See also: <a href="/wiki/Name_of_Canada#Adoption_of_Dominion" title="Name of Canada">Name of Canada \xc2\xa7&#160;Adoption of Dominion</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Image2a-88"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Image2a_88-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The Australian and South African prime ministers, <a href="/wiki/Billy_Hughes" title="Billy Hughes">Billy Hughes</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis_Botha" title="Louis Botha">Louis Botha</a>, stand first and second from the right; the Canadian delegate, <a href="/wiki/George_Eulas_Foster" title="George Eulas Foster">Sir George Foster</a>, stands fourth from left. The representatives of New Zealand and Newfoundland are not shown.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Image3-89"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Image3_89-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The figures in the photo are, back row, left to right: <a href="/wiki/Walter_Stanley_Monroe" title="Walter Stanley Monroe">Walter Stanley Monroe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect" title="Prime Minister of Newfoundland">Prime Minister of Newfoundland</a>; <a href="/wiki/Gordon_Coates" title="Gordon Coates">Gordon Coates</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_New_Zealand" title="Prime Minister of New Zealand">Prime Minister of New Zealand</a>; <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Bruce" title="Stanley Bruce">Stanley Bruce</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">Prime Minister of Australia</a>; <a href="/wiki/J._B._M._Hertzog" title="J. B. M. Hertzog">James Hertzog</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_South_Africa" title="Prime Minister of South Africa">Prime Minister of South Africa</a>, and <a href="/wiki/W._T._Cosgrave" title="W. T. Cosgrave">W. T. Cosgrave</a>, <a href="/wiki/President_of_the_Executive_Council_of_the_Irish_Free_State" title="President of the Executive Council of the Irish Free State">President of the Executive Council of the Irish Free State</a>; front row, left to right: <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Baldwin" title="Stanley Baldwin">Stanley Baldwin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="Prime Minister of the United Kingdom">Prime Minister of the United Kingdom</a>; the King; and <a href="/wiki/William_Lyon_Mackenzie_King" title="William Lyon Mackenzie King">William Lyon Mackenzie King</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Prime Minister of Canada</a>.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Haldane-96"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Haldane_96-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Richard_Haldane,_1st_Viscount_Haldane" title="Richard Haldane, 1st Viscount Haldane">The Viscount Haldane</a> said in 1919 that in Australia the Crown "acts in self-governing States on the initiative and advice of its own ministers in these States."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Balf-101"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Balf_101-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">The ministers in attendance at the Imperial Conference agreed that: "In our opinion it is an essential consequence of the equality of status existing among the members of the British Commonwealth of Nations that the Governor General of a Dominion is the representative of the Crown, holding in all essential respects the same position in relation to the administration of public affairs in the Dominion as is held by His Majesty the King in Great Britain, and that he is not the representative or agent of His Majesty\'s Government in Great Britain or of any Department of that Government".<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Anti-108"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Anti_108-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">P.E. Corbett in 1940 questioned whether there were any existing terms that could be used to describe any or all of the "possessions of the British Crown,"<sup id="cite_ref-corbett1_30-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-corbett1-30">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> while <a href="/wiki/Scotland" title="Scotland">Scottish</a> constitutional lawyer <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Berriedale_Keith" title="Arthur Berriedale Keith">Arthur Berriedale Keith</a> warned before 1930 that "the suggestion that the King can act directly on the advice of Dominion Ministers is a constitutional monstrosity, which would be fatal to the security of the position of the Crown."<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup></span>\n</li>\n</ol></div></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Commonwealth_realm&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-2"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-2">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Figures totalled from member state profiles at the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> secretariat, rounded to the nearest 100,000.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-3"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-3">^</a></b></span> <span
